  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2e73d72e-2c9c-4f99-ba00-50e7c4334a97'
      });
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9575103291611356035"><strong>From the legendary creator of <em>Where the Sidewalk Ends, A Light in the Attic, Falling Up,</em> and <em>The Giving Tree</em> comes an unforgettable new character in children's literature: Runny Babbit.</strong><br/><br/><em>Runny Babbit</em> is Shel Silverstein's hilarious and <em>New York Times-</em>bestselling book of spoonerisms—words or phrases with letters or syllables swapped: bunny rabbit becomes Runny Babbit.<br/><br/>Welcome </span>
  <span id="freeText9575103291611356035" style="display:none"><strong>From the legendary creator of <em>Where the Sidewalk Ends, A Light in the Attic, Falling Up,</em> and <em>The Giving Tree</em> comes an unforgettable new character in children's literature: Runny Babbit.</strong><br /><br /><em>Runny Babbit</em> is Shel Silverstein's hilarious and <em>New York Times-</em>bestselling book of spoonerisms—words or phrases with letters or syllables swapped: bunny rabbit becomes Runny Babbit.<br /><br />Welcome to the world of Runny Babbit and his friends Toe Jurtle, Skertie Gunk, Rirty Dat, Dungry Hog, Snerry Jake, and many others who speak a topsy-turvy language all their own.<br /><br /><em>So if you say, "Let's bead a rook<br />That's billy as can se,"<br />You're talkin' Runny Babbit talk,<br />Just like mim and he.</em><br /><br />And don't miss <em>Runny Babbit Returns</em>, the new book from Shel Silverstein!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9575103291611356035" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('rating_details_tip').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

</script>  </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135653615" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/135653615?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=humour">humour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=gift-book">gift-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer135653615" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4567566112089064498">Definitely a very creative work of <b>Shel Silverstein</b> (1930-1999) who is also the author of the 1964 book, "The Giving Tree" that I enjoyed so much I bought copies of which and gave away to my friends. I think I did that in 2001 not knowing that he just died a couple of years back. I also only learned that he's already dead by reading the Wiki while composing this review. Felt so sad.<br/><br/>The story's main protagonist is <b>Runny Babbit</b> whose actual name is Bunny Rabbit but for unknown reason he and all th</span>
  <span id="freeText4567566112089064498" style="display:none">Definitely a very creative work of <b>Shel Silverstein</b> (1930-1999) who is also the author of the 1964 book, "The Giving Tree" that I enjoyed so much I bought copies of which and gave away to my friends. I think I did that in 2001 not knowing that he just died a couple of years back. I also only learned that he's already dead by reading the Wiki while composing this review. Felt so sad.<br /><br />The story's main protagonist is <b>Runny Babbit</b> whose actual name is Bunny Rabbit but for unknown reason he and all the animals in the story, i.e., Toe Jurtle, Skertie Gunk, Rirty Dat, Dungry Hog, Snerry Jake, etc., interchange the first letter of the two words of their names and most the other two-word phrases when they talk to each other. I had to adjust a bit at the start but eventually gained speed halfway the book. Just like any typical children's book, the story is composed of several independent funny events in the life of Runny Babbit and his friends and each story varies in my laugh barometer from mild, medium and outright funny. Hey, some are even cheesy or heartwarming (which should be for parents to enjoy).<br /><br />The drawings are hilarious! They are in black-and-white and done in simple way but the imagination of the illustrator is just awesome. They effectively complement the free-verse poems (that tell the stories). My favorites are "His Kajesty, the Ming" (pp. 19) with Runny's friends lining up while bowing down to him in respect and "Killy the Bird" (pp. 45) with the same set of friends lining up in surrender to Runny atop a horse with his gun. You should see their faces. Soo cute!<br /><br />During Christmastime, I normally give away to my friends and officemates the books that I enjoyed but do not plan to re-read. Many of those books are children's books since nobody in my family is interested to read that genre. However, this one I will keep for future re-reads. Also I still have to play the CD. Since my daughter is already 15 going 16, I think I will reserve that one when I already have grandchildren hopefully around 10 years from now.<br /><br /><i>You who gave me this last Dec 18: you know who you are and I thank you for the friendship that I will be remembering everytime I see this book. Thanks for a wonderful book!</i> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4567566112089064498" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6220364867115637318"><b>* * * Read & reviewed with my niece Emma * * *</b><br/><br/>Nope. Wasn't working for us. We just weren't in the mood for the silly wordplay. For example, the subtitle to <i>Runny Babbit</i> is <i>A Billy Sook</i>. <br/><br/>Maybe we'll give this another shot at another time, but this time around both Emma and I found this too annoying to read, regardless of how short it is. A shame really. I'd hoped for more from a Shel Silverstein. I expect him to knock it out of the park every time. <br/><br/></span>
  <span id="freeText6220364867115637318" style="display:none"><b>* * * Read &amp; reviewed with my niece Emma * * *</b><br /><br />Nope. Wasn't working for us. We just weren't in the mood for the silly wordplay. For example, the subtitle to <i>Runny Babbit</i> is <i>A Billy Sook</i>. <br /><br />Maybe we'll give this another shot at another time, but this time around both Emma and I found this too annoying to read, regardless of how short it is. A shame really. I'd hoped for more from a Shel Silverstein. I expect him to knock it out of the park every time. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2743304337117950721">This is another book I read to my brother before bedtime. It is a silly book of poems that switch around the first letters of two words, creating funny sounds and sentences. <br/>For example: <br/><i>"Runny be quimble <br/>Runny be nick <br/>Runny cump over the jandlestick" </i><br/>He enjoyed it very much and I'm sure any kid would, too.   <span id="freeText2743304337117950721" style="display:none">This is another book I read to my brother before bedtime. It is a silly book of poems that switch around the first letters of two words, creating funny sounds and sentences. <br />For example: <br /><i>"Runny be quimble <br />Runny be nick <br />Runny cump over the jandlestick" </i><br />He enjoyed it very much and I'm sure any kid would, too. I took a star away from my usual four stars though, because I found it very odd that the characters said such mean things to each other. For example, all of Runny's friends insult him for eating too much and being 'fat' (it's a bit harsh). I felt compelled to remind my brother that their behavior isn't kind and shouldn't be reenacted. <br /> </span>

<div id="review_381323680" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381323680" />
    <a title="Skylar Burris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/710201-skylar-burris"><img alt="Skylar Burris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1449959508p2/710201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381323680?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skylar Burris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skylar Burris" href="/user/show/710201-skylar-burris">Skylar Burris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/710201-skylar-burris?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/710201-skylar-burris?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/710201-skylar-burris?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381323680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9932108419204298877">This was published posthumously, as, I believe, was Shel Silverstein’s first collection of poems (Don’t Bump the Glump), and I am glad to have a chance, as an adult, to read two more books from the pen of my favorite childhood poet. In many ways, Runny Babbit is a typical collection of Shel Silverstein poetry, but with two differences from his norm: they all deal with the same central character (Runny Babbit), and the letters of some words are switched. <br/><br/>I read this together with my daughter, and</span>
  <span id="freeText9932108419204298877" style="display:none">This was published posthumously, as, I believe, was Shel Silverstein’s first collection of poems (Don’t Bump the Glump), and I am glad to have a chance, as an adult, to read two more books from the pen of my favorite childhood poet. In many ways, Runny Babbit is a typical collection of Shel Silverstein poetry, but with two differences from his norm: they all deal with the same central character (Runny Babbit), and the letters of some words are switched. <br /><br />I read this together with my daughter, and she enjoyed “decoding” the poems for a while. I thought it was a good exercise in phonics and reading for her to try to figure out what the words were supposed to be. She could do it about 60 percent of the time on her own, and the other forty percent of the time I’d nudge her with “switch the __ and the __” to help her along. After a while, she got tired of this exercise, and I began reading the poems to her more quickly “in translation,” as the words should be. I think if you read them as they are written, it is too hard for a kid to get the jokes within the poems themselves (though some kids will simply laugh at the joke of silly sounding words), but if you do the switcheroo as you read, many of the poems are actually quite clever of their own accord, and several have the trademark Shel Silverstein funny twist. (I especially liked the one where Runny Babit’s friends left with chicken pox.) <br /><br />Reading this book requires more effort and interaction than is typical for our nighttime reading, and I probably would not want to do it again, but as an exercise in thought, and for the general quality of the poems, I give the stook four bars.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9932108419204298877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_761802894" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/761802894" />
    <a title="L13_F Sandra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2301896-l13-f-sandra"><img alt="L13_F Sandra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379855591p2/2301896.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/761802894?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="L13_F Sandra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="L13_F Sandra" href="/user/show/2301896-l13-f-sandra">L13_F Sandra</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2301896-l13-f-sandra?shelf=poetry">poetry</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer761802894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8668987505306091294">I listened to this on CD while reading the book at the same time. It was read by Dennis Locorriere who has sort of a scratchy voice but he made it very entertaining. I tried to listen to it without looking at the book but it was so difficult to understand without seeing the pictures and words. It sounded like "Jive Talk" and there were a few parts that sounded like the reader was swearing like when he said "fookin' for a light!" in the poem Killy The Bid. This made up language took some getting </span>
  <span id="freeText8668987505306091294" style="display:none">I listened to this on CD while reading the book at the same time. It was read by Dennis Locorriere who has sort of a scratchy voice but he made it very entertaining. I tried to listen to it without looking at the book but it was so difficult to understand without seeing the pictures and words. It sounded like "Jive Talk" and there were a few parts that sounded like the reader was swearing like when he said "fookin' for a light!" in the poem Killy The Bid. This made up language took some getting used to but after I figured out that Shel Silverstein just switched some letters from two separate words to create new words, I got the hang of it. I still needed the book to see the words however. That made it a lot easier to comprehend. I think my favorite poem was Runny's Rittle Leminders and there were about 30 post-it-notes on the wall of reminders of what Runny should remember to do. I guess I picked up on all those quickly as they were being read because they are things I say to my own kids but in English of course; bake your med, trush your beeth,fash your wace and say thease and plank you. <br /><br />I think kids would enjoy trying to read these aloud because they are kind of like tongue twisters. I would recommend this book for 4th grade up. Any younger, they might have difficulties trying to comprehend what they are saying. I think it would be a fun activity to take a regular poem and change the letters around to make it a silly poem like the ones in this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8668987505306091294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_489746753" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/489746753" />
    <a title="Katherine Dyson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11499836-katherine-dyson"><img alt="Katherine Dyson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/489746753?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katherine Dyson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katherine Dyson" href="/user/show/11499836-katherine-dyson">Katherine Dyson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer489746753" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4950766376628511809">This book certainly kept me entertained while I tried to read the jumbled up words and try and make sense of the sentences I was reading. <br/>This story is about a rabbit on a simple adventure, however the clever quirk that the author inhibits within the story is to change the first letter of certain words with another letter of a word e.g runny Babbit.<br/>This book would be great to use as a game during a phonics lesson or just at the end of the day before the children go home. They could challenge the</span>
  <span id="freeText4950766376628511809" style="display:none">This book certainly kept me entertained while I tried to read the jumbled up words and try and make sense of the sentences I was reading. <br />This story is about a rabbit on a simple adventure, however the clever quirk that the author inhibits within the story is to change the first letter of certain words with another letter of a word e.g runny Babbit.<br />This book would be great to use as a game during a phonics lesson or just at the end of the day before the children go home. They could challenge themselves to who can read a whole page correctly in the shortest time. Although all the words are not correct, due to the authors quirkiness, it still promotes the learning of phonics as the children would need to use their knowledge to read the new words created. <br />A visualiser could be used or the page could be written up on an IWB for all the class to check the child's articulation.<br />I would recommend this book for teaching year one upwards, older pupils could even create their own runny Babbit style book. </span>

<div id="review_53924295" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53924295" />
    <a title="Dani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1016719-dani"><img alt="Dani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1512501657p2/1016719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53924295?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dani" href="/user/show/1016719-dani">Dani</a>
      </span>

          added it



          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Parents and teachers with struggling reading students</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53924295" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14111429700499922874">For every frustrated kid learning how to read - make the parents read this one aloud so they'll get a first-hand taste at how hard it really is sounding out those confusing letters! This book can be the turning point for a struggling learner, and at the very least, will develop some empathy on the part of adults who have forgotten how confusing language is. A sensitive and hysterically funny book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer554304716" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15574845491552717827">I know that I've read this one before, in my quest to expose our girls to the wonderful works of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/435477.Shel_Silverstein' title='Shel Silverstein' rel='nofollow noopener'>Shel Silverstein</a>. But when I tried to read it aloud with our girls, I realized right away that they were too young to understand the nuances and the humor of the mixed up words. So I waited a few more years before we tried again. <br/><br/>This is not an easy book to read aloud, but it's certainly entertaining and our girls are now at a perfect age to understand the humor and nuances of the semantic acrobatics</span>
  <span id="freeText15574845491552717827" style="display:none">I know that I've read this one before, in my quest to expose our girls to the wonderful works of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/435477.Shel_Silverstein" title="Shel Silverstein" rel="nofollow noopener">Shel Silverstein</a>. But when I tried to read it aloud with our girls, I realized right away that they were too young to understand the nuances and the humor of the mixed up words. So I waited a few more years before we tried again. <br /><br />This is not an easy book to read aloud, but it's certainly entertaining and our girls are now at a perfect age to understand the humor and nuances of the semantic acrobatics. Still, it took us some time to read the whole thing. We would talk about the mixed up words and our girls would often say the 'correct' phrase after I read the mixed up one. We enjoyed reading this book together, but it's not our favorite. </span>

<div id="review_1090929725" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090929725" />
    <a title="Chrissie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33603612-chrissie"><img alt="Chrissie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546979222p2/33603612.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090929725?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chrissie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chrissie" href="/user/show/33603612-chrissie">Chrissie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33603612-chrissie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33603612-chrissie?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33603612-chrissie?shelf=childrens-books">childrens-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33603612-chrissie?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090929725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8700874767249404932"><b>Runny Babbit</b> is a cute and silly book that'll get you quite tongue-twisted, chock full of purposeful spoonerisms—a verbal error in which a speaker accidentally transposes the initial sounds or letters of two or more words, often to humorous effect.<br/><br/>This one was a favorite with my kids when they were young, producing giggles when you get it wrong just as often as when you get it right.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117447082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12675215417075979920">Unfortunately I was not impressed by Runny Babbit. More like listening to gibberish than anything else. I suppose it may be better in print. I just happen to get a free copy on audiobook. Definitely not one of my favorite Shel Silverstein poems. Though I imagine in print the illustrations would be cute. </span>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8fEe/5orwbDjDS5AuXDWIV1IsXMD0figHSYrg90JV8bvldpMwN2wa+JFF3LtRHT6R1yNXwu78iD0RJ0Etx/PoA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('F2bjpQA14MN10aYM+uUstJNdaKGQAByPktM9aA2kCE8JAicWWsORGHSZnz6u0Y5viUlUjZhqFg97sYvvZ7KQKQ==')})
  }
//]]>
